Fortunately, the Dualshock 3 is one of the most comfortable PS3 controllers I have tested, if not the most comfortable controller out there on the market right now. The design is perfect for your hands. All the buttons are evenly placed and are all in the easy reach. The controller is symmetrical, rather than other gaming controllers. The symmetrical button layout feels much better to use in gaming, especially if you're a huge player FPS games or any time of games with the use of both Analog Sticks. This controller is also very light, even with the Vibration. They're even light enough to use the controller with one hand without any struggle at all.   The build quality on these are also very good. I've had mine since the day it was released, about 3 years ago, and it still works like new. I've done a lot of button mashing, dropped the controller a few times, and abused the analog sticks more than anyone should, but it still feels good. These controllers are very hard to break. For my personal use, my analog sticks are a little firmer than the average controller, but that's because of the treatment I had them under. An average player should be fine. All the buttons are sturdy, and the controller is firmly built, so you shouldn't have a problem.   Battery Life is also a huge factor, and they're fantastic with these. The controller comes with a short USB 2.0 Wire which you connect to any USB Port (You're PS3, Computer, or USB - Power Outlet) and it charges. From completely dead to full takes about 30 minutes at most, and will last you for weeks! The PS3 XMB Screen will indicate how much battery life you have left, and when the battery is getting low, the Red Light on the back will start blinking, but even then, you can still game for about three more hours before it's completely dead.   So how does it feel in game? Well I play from a variety of games. Racing, Platformers, Shooters, Adventure, Stealth etc. The controller naturally feels the great. All the buttons are great, and these are the best Analog Sticks you can get on any gaming controller! They have lots of grip and they're dead accurate! The vibration is also great. They definitely don't match the amount of Vibration the Dualshock 2 offered, but it's still above satisfactory. All of the soft buttons, such as the X, SQUARE, TRIANGLE, CIRCLE, R1, and L2, all have varied activation depending on how hard you press. For example, in Gran Turismo 5, if you press the X button lightly, it will do a slow acceleration, but press the controller firmly, and you will accelerate much faster. Same goes with most other games such as MGS4 and its CQC controls. The sixaxis is also a nice little feature. Most games really don't use it much, but for the games that do, the Sixaxis is very accurate and fun to use one you get used to it. Even though this controller is great, I have one complaint about it, and that's the R2 and L2 button. They have a Convex shape, so if your hands get sweaty, they'll easily slip off. Another complaint is that the L2 and R2 buttons aren't as accurate and doesn't have as much vary when you half press them as compared to the Xbox 360 controller.  Other than the L2 and R2 buttons, these are the best controllers money can buy!

In Cinder's hometown, New Beijing to be exact, the earth has experienced, and is still experiencing a horrible plague.  Imagine the Black Death in the Middle Ages to the extreme as this virus hit the whole of earth's population.  And even after years later, it's still spreading.  Unfortunately for Cinder, this isn't even half her problems.  She's also a cyborg.  Somewhere along the way she lost her hand and foot, which is now made from metal, and connected to her nervous system.  So technically she is still part human, but to full humans...cyborg's are just robots without emotions, and below them.  Neighboring merchants give her evil glares, or at least the ones who know about her extremities, and the only one who can even remotely be called a friend is her step-sister Peony, and Cinder's robot friend Iko. Kai's hand in marriage.  Cinder's chance for fleeing her step-mother draws near, but yet, she has choices to make.  Either escape the cruelty of her step-mother, or stay to help a friend.  In the end, even a cyborg has to rely on their heart.<br /><br />Cinder is a totally transparent tale as it is a retelling of the Cinderella story minus the mice and fairy godmother.  Add in a dystopian world where androids and cyborgs are common place, a disease is spreading over the entire earth killing thousands, and you've definitely got a new take on a classic story.  I truly enjoyed all the characters, which is saying something.  Cinder was not a weakling, and often stood up to her step mom, and while you might think that her being a cyborg would nix the emotion, it really only enhanced it.  I felt for her when she couldn't cry, and even envied her the ability to not blush.  Prince Kai was written well, a very down to earth person with the world on his shoulders.  You can tell he didn't want/wasn't ready for his role as King, but yet he took the burden willingly.  The plot on the other hand was very easily figured out.  I won't give it away here, but I mean, within the first two chapters, you know everything that is going to happen.  But even that still didn't take away from the story.  And more importantly, while I did know what was going to happen here, I'm at a loss as to what will occur in the next book!
